Nevertheless, Ireland retained its own parliament, becoming an independent state in 1642-1649 (<a href="/wiki/Confederate_Ireland" title="Confederate Ireland">Confederate Ireland</a>), and again in 1688-91. Only warfare such as the <a href="/wiki/Williamite_War_in_Ireland" title="Williamite War in Ireland">Williamite War in Ireland</a> and subsequent occupation enabled the English crown from 1692, and successive British states from 1707, to retain the country.</p>
<p>In 1800, as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Rebellion_of_1798" title="Irish Rebellion of 1798">Irish Rebellion of 1798</a>, the Act of Union merged the kingdom of Great Britain and the kingdom of Ireland into the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland</a>. The whole island of Ireland continued to be a part of the United Kingdom until 1922, when what is now the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> won independence as the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a>, a separate Dominion within the Commonwealth. The Irish Free State was renamed <a href="/wiki/%C3%89ire" title="Éire">Éire</a> (or "Ireland") in 1937, and in 1949 declared itself a republic, left the Commonwealth and severed all ties with the monarchy. <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> remained within the Union. In 1927, the United Kingdom changed its name to the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland, while the monarch's style for the next twenty years became "of Great Britain, Ireland and the British Dominions beyond the Seas, King, Defender of the Faith, Emperor of India".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_status">Modern status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Modern status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 1990s, <a href="/wiki/Republicanism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Republicanism in the United Kingdom">Republicanism in the United Kingdom</a> grew, partly on account of negative publicity associated with the Royal Family (for instance, immediately following the death of <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana, Princess of Wales</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> However, recent polls show that around 70–80% of the British public support the continuation of the monarchy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_role">Religious role</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religious role">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The sovereign is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Governor" title="Supreme Governor">Supreme Governor</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Established_church" title="Established church">established</a> <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a>. Archbishops and bishops are appointed by the monarch, on the advice of the Prime Minister, who chooses the appointee from a list of nominees prepared by a Church Commission. The Crown's role in the Church of England is titular; the most senior clergyman, the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a>, is the spiritual leader of the Church and of the worldwide <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Communion" title="Anglican Communion">Anglican Communion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The monarch takes an oath to preserve <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> and he or she holds the power to appoint the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_High_Commissioner" title="Lord High Commissioner">Lord High Commissioner</a> to the Church's <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_Church_of_Scotland" title="General Assembly of the Church of Scotland">General Assembly</a>, but otherwise plays no part in its governance, and enjoys no powers over it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The Sovereign plays no formal role in the disestablished <a href="/wiki/Church_in_Wales" title="Church in Wales">Church in Wales</a> or <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Ireland" title="Church of Ireland">Church of Ireland</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Succession">Succession</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Succession">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Succession_to_the_British_throne" title="Succession to the British throne">Succession to the British throne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_British_monarch" title="Coronation of the British monarch">Coronation of the British monarch</a></div>
<p>The relationship between the Commonwealth realms is such that any change to the laws governing succession to the shared throne requires the unanimous consent of all the realms. Succession is governed by statutes such as the <a href="/wiki/Bill_of_Rights_1689" title="Bill of Rights 1689">Bill of Rights 1689</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Settlement_1701" title="Act of Settlement 1701">Act of Settlement 1701</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union 1707</a>. The rules of succession may only be changed by an <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Parliament" title="Act of Parliament">Act of Parliament</a>; it is not possible for an individual to renounce his or her right of succession. The Act of Settlement restricts the succession to the legitimate Protestant descendants of <a href="/wiki/Sophia_of_Hanover" title="Sophia of Hanover">Sophia of Hanover</a> (1630–1714), a granddaughter of <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">James I</a>.</p>
<p>Upon the death of a sovereign, his or her heir immediately and automatically succeeds (hence the phrase "<a href="/wiki/The_king_is_dead,_long_live_the_king!" title="The king is dead, long live the king!">The king is dead, long live the king!</a>"), and the accession of the new sovereign is publicly proclaimed by an <a href="/wiki/Accession_Council" title="Accession Council">Accession Council</a> that meets at <a href="/wiki/St_James%27s_Palace" title="St James's Palace">St James's Palace</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-accessioncouncil_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-accessioncouncil-86">[86]</a></sup> Upon their accession, a new sovereign is required by law to make and subscribe several oaths: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accession_Declaration" title="Accession Declaration">Accession Declaration</a> as first required by the Bill of Rights, and an oath that they will "maintain and preserve" the Church of Scotland settlement as required by the Act of Union. The monarch is usually <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_British_monarch" title="Coronation of the British monarch">crowned</a> in <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a>, normally by the Archbishop of Canterbury. A coronation is not necessary for a sovereign to reign; indeed, the ceremony usually takes place many months after accession to allow sufficient time for its preparation and for a period of mourning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>After an individual ascends the throne, he or she reigns until death. The only voluntary abdication, that of <a href="/wiki/Edward_VIII" title="Edward VIII">Edward VIII</a>, had to be authorised by a special Act of Parliament, <a href="/wiki/His_Majesty%27s_Declaration_of_Abdication_Act_1936" title="His Majesty's Declaration of Abdication Act 1936">His Majesty's Declaration of Abdication Act 1936</a>. The last monarch involuntarily removed from power was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_VII_and_II" title="James VII and II">James VII and II</a>, who fled into exile in 1688 during the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Restrictions_by_gender_and_religion">Restrictions by gender and religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Restrictions by gender and religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Succession_to_the_Crown_Act_2013" title="Succession to the Crown Act 2013">Succession to the Crown Act 2013</a></div>
<p>Succession was largely governed by <a href="/wiki/Primogeniture" title="Primogeniture">male-preference cognatic primogeniture</a>, under which sons inherit before daughters, and elder children inherit before younger ones of the same gender. The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>, announced at the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Heads_of_Government_Meeting_2011" title="Commonwealth Heads of Government Meeting 2011">Commonwealth Heads of Government Meeting 2011</a> that all 16 <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a>, including the United Kingdom, had agreed to abolish the gender-preference rule for anyone born after the date of the meeting, 28 October 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> They also agreed that future monarchs would no longer be prohibited from marrying a Roman Catholic – a law which dated from the Act of Settlement 1701. However, since the monarch is also the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Governor_of_the_Church_of_England" title="Supreme Governor of the Church of England">Supreme Governor of the Church of England</a>, the law which prohibits a Roman Catholic from acceding to the throne remains. The necessary UK legislation making the changes received the royal assent on 25 April 2013 and was brought into force in March 2015 after the equivalent legislation was approved in all the other Commonwealth realms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>Only individuals who are Protestants may inherit the Crown. Roman Catholics are prohibited from succeeding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> An individual thus disabled from inheriting the Crown is deemed "naturally dead" for succession purposes, and the disqualification does not extend to the individual's legitimate descendants.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regency">Regency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Regency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regency_Acts" title="Regency Acts">Regency Acts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Counsellor_of_State" title="Counsellor of State">Counsellor of State</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Regency_Acts" title="Regency Acts">Regency Acts</a> allow for regencies in the event of a monarch who is a minor or who is physically or mentally incapacitated. When a regency is necessary, the next qualified individual in the line of succession automatically becomes regent, unless they themselves are a minor or incapacitated. Special provisions were made for Queen Elizabeth II by the Regency Act 1953, which stated that <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">the Duke of Edinburgh</a> (the Queen's husband) could act as regent in these circumstances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regact53_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-regact53-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>During a temporary physical infirmity or an absence from the kingdom, the sovereign may temporarily delegate some of his or her functions to <a href="/wiki/Counsellor_of_State" title="Counsellor of State">Counsellors of State</a>, the monarch's spouse and the first four adults in the line of succession. The present Counsellors of State are: the Duke of Edinburgh, the <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Prince William, Duke of Cambridge">Duke of Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Harry" title="Prince Harry">Prince Harry</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Andrew,_Duke_of_York" title="Prince Andrew, Duke of York">Duke of York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Finances_of_the_British_Royal_Family" title="Finances of the British Royal Family">Finances of the British Royal Family</a></div>
<p>Until 1760 the monarch met all official expenses from hereditary revenues, which included the profits of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Estate" title="Crown Estate">Crown Estate</a> (the royal property portfolio). <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George III of the United Kingdom">King George III</a> agreed to surrender the hereditary revenues of the Crown in return for the <a href="/wiki/Civil_list#United_Kingdom" title="Civil list">Civil List</a>, and this arrangement persisted until 2012. An annual Property Services <a href="/wiki/Grant-in-aid" title="Grant-in-aid">Grant-in-aid</a> paid for the upkeep of the royal residences, and an annual Royal Travel Grant-in-Aid paid for travel. The Civil List covered most expenses, including those for staffing, state visits, public engagements, and official entertainment. Its size was fixed by Parliament every 10 years; any money saved was carried forward to the next 10-year period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cl_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-cl-95">[95]</a></sup> From 2012 until 2020, the Civil List and Grants-in-Aid are to be replaced with a single <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sovereign_Grant" title="Sovereign Grant">Sovereign Grant</a>, which will be set at 15% of the revenues generated by the Crown Estate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Crown Estate is one of the largest property owners in the United Kingdom, with holdings of £7.3 billion in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> It is held in trust, and cannot be sold or owned by the Sovereign in a private capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> In modern times, the profits surrendered from the Crown Estate to the Treasury have exceeded the Civil List and Grants-in-Aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cl_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-cl-95">[95]</a></sup> For example, the Crown Estate produced £200 million in the financial year 2007–8, whereas reported parliamentary funding for the monarch was £40 million during the same period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>Like the Crown Estate, the land and assets of the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Lancaster" title="Duchy of Lancaster">Duchy of Lancaster</a>, a property portfolio valued at £383 million in 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> are held in trust. The revenues of the Duchy form part of the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Purse" title="Privy Purse">Privy Purse</a>, and are used for expenses not borne by the parliamentary grants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Cornwall" title="Duchy of Cornwall">Duchy of Cornwall</a> is a similar estate held in trust to meet the expenses of the monarch's eldest son. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Collection" title="Royal Collection">Royal Collection</a>, which includes artworks and the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Jewels_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Crown Jewels of the United Kingdom">Crown Jewels</a>, is not owned by the Sovereign personally and is held <a href="/wiki/Trust_law" title="Trust law">in trust</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> as are the occupied palaces in the United Kingdom such as <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Castle" title="Windsor Castle">Windsor Castle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-res_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-res-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>The sovereign is subject to indirect taxes such as <a href="/wiki/Value-added_tax_(United_Kingdom)" title="Value-added tax (United Kingdom)">value-added tax</a>, and since 1993 the Queen has paid <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Capital_gains_tax" title="Capital gains tax">capital gains tax</a> on personal income. Parliamentary grants to the Sovereign are not treated as income as they are solely for official expenditure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Republicans estimate that the real cost of the monarchy, including security and potential income not claimed by the state, such as profits from the duchies of Lancaster and Cornwall and rent of Buckingham Palace and Windsor Castle, is £334 million a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Estimates of the Queen's wealth vary, depending on whether assets owned by her personally or held in trust for the nation are included. <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine estimated her wealth at US$450 million in 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> but no official figure is available. In 1993, the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chamberlain" title="Lord Chamberlain">Lord Chamberlain</a> said estimates of £100 million were "grossly overstated".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jock_Colville" title="Jock Colville">Jock Colville</a>, who was her former private secretary and a director of her bank, <a href="/wiki/Coutts" title="Coutts">Coutts</a>, estimated her wealth in 1971 at £2 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> (the equivalent of about £25 million today<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-110">[110]</a></sup>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Residences">Residences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Residences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Buckingham_Palace_2007_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Buckingham_Palace_2007_2.jpg/220px-Buckingham_Palace_2007_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Buckingham_Palace_2007_2.jpg/330px-Buckingham_Palace_2007_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Buckingham_Palace_2007_2.jpg/440px-Buckingham_Palace_2007_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Buckingham_Palace_2007_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Buckingham Palace, the monarch's principal residence</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wfm_holyrood_palace.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="460" data-file-width="800" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Wfm_holyrood_palace.jpg/220px-Wfm_holyrood_palace.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Wfm_holyrood_palace.jpg/330px-Wfm_holyrood_palace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Wfm_holyrood_palace.jpg/440px-Wfm_holyrood_palace.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wfm_holyrood_palace.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Holyrood Palace, the monarch's official Scottish residence</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_royal_residences" title="List of British royal residences">List of British royal residences</a></div>
<p>The Sovereign's official residence in London is <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a>. It is the site of most state banquets, investitures, royal christenings and other ceremonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BuckinghamPalace_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-BuckinghamPalace-111">[111]</a></sup> Another official residence is <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Castle" title="Windsor Castle">Windsor Castle</a>, the largest occupied castle in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WindsorCastle_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-WindsorCastle-112">[112]</a></sup> which is used principally at weekends, Easter and during <a href="/wiki/Ascot_Racecourse" title="Ascot Racecourse">Royal Ascot</a>, an annual race meeting that is part of the <a href="/wiki/Season_(society)" title="Season (society)">social calendar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WindsorCastle_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-WindsorCastle-112">[112]</a></sup> The Sovereign's official residence in Scotland is the <a href="/wiki/Holyrood_Palace" title="Holyrood Palace">Palace of Holyroodhouse</a> in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>. The monarch stays at Holyrood for at least one week each year, and when visiting Scotland on state occasions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holyroodhouse_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holyroodhouse-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>Historically, the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Westminster" title="Palace of Westminster">Palace of Westminster</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a> were the main residences of the English Sovereign until Henry VIII acquired the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Whitehall" title="Palace of Whitehall">Palace of Whitehall</a>. Whitehall was destroyed by fire in 1698, leading to a shift to <a href="/wiki/St_James%27s_Palace" title="St James's Palace">St James's Palace</a>. Although replaced as the monarch's primary London residence by Buckingham Palace in 1837, St James's is still the senior palace<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StJamessPalace_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-StJamessPalace-114">[114]</a></sup> and remains the ceremonial Royal residence. For example, foreign ambassadors are accredited to the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_St_James%27s" title="Court of St James's">Court of St James's</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BuckinghamPalace_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-BuckinghamPalace-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> and the Palace is the site of the meeting of the <a href="/wiki/Accession_Council" title="Accession Council">Accession Council</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-accessioncouncil_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-accessioncouncil-86">[86]</a></sup> It is also used by other members of the Royal Family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StJamessPalace_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-StJamessPalace-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other residences include <a href="/wiki/Clarence_House" title="Clarence House">Clarence House</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kensington_Palace" title="Kensington Palace">Kensington Palace</a>. The palaces belong to the Crown; they are held in trust for future rulers, and cannot be sold by the monarch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sandringham_House" title="Sandringham House">Sandringham House</a> in <a href="/wiki/Norfolk" title="Norfolk">Norfolk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balmoral_Castle" title="Balmoral Castle">Balmoral Castle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Aberdeenshire_(historic)" title="Aberdeenshire (historic)">Aberdeenshire</a> are privately owned by the Queen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-res_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-res-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style">Style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Style_of_the_British_sovereign" title="Style of the British sovereign">Style of the British sovereign</a></div>
<p>The present Sovereign's full style and title is "Elizabeth the Second, by the Grace of God, of the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland and of Her other Realms and Territories Queen, Head of the Commonwealth, Defender of the Faith".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The title "<a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Commonwealth" title="Head of the Commonwealth">Head of the Commonwealth</a>" is held by the Queen personally, and is not vested in the British Crown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hoc_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-hoc-72">[72]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_X" title="Pope Leo X">Pope Leo X</a> first granted the title "<a href="/wiki/Fidei_defensor" title="Fidei defensor">Defender of the Faith</a>" to King Henry VIII in 1521, rewarding him for his support of the Papacy during the early years of the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>, particularly for his book the <a href="/wiki/Defence_of_the_Seven_Sacraments" title="Defence of the Seven Sacraments">Defence of the Seven Sacraments</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> After Henry broke from the Roman Church, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_III" title="Pope Paul III">Pope Paul III</a> revoked the grant, but Parliament passed a law authorising its continued use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Sovereign is known as "His Majesty" or "Her Majesty". The form "Britannic Majesty" appears in international treaties and on passports to differentiate the British monarch from foreign rulers. The monarch chooses his or her <a href="/wiki/Regnal_name" title="Regnal name">regnal name</a>, not necessarily his or her first name – <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">King George VI</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_VII" title="Edward VII">King Edward VII</a> and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> did not use their first names.</p>
<p>If only one monarch has used a particular name, no ordinal is used; for example, Queen Victoria is not known as "Victoria I", and ordinals are not used for English monarchs who reigned before the Norman conquest of England. The question of whether numbering for British monarchs is based on previous English or Scottish monarchs was raised in 1953 when Scottish nationalists challenged the Queen's use of "Elizabeth II", on the grounds that there had never been an "Elizabeth I" in Scotland. In <i><a href="/wiki/MacCormick_v_Lord_Advocate" title="MacCormick v Lord Advocate">MacCormick v Lord Advocate</a></i>, the Scottish <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Session" title="Court of Session">Court of Session</a> ruled against the plaintiffs, finding that the Queen's title was a matter of her own choice and prerogative. The Home Secretary told the House of Commons that monarchs since the Acts of Union had consistently used the higher of the English and Scottish ordinals, which in the applicable four cases has been the English ordinal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> The Prime Minister confirmed this practice, but noted that "neither The Queen nor her advisers could seek to bind their successors".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Future monarchs will apply this policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>Traditionally, the signature of the monarch includes their regnal name but not ordinal, followed by the letter R, which stands for <i>rex</i> or <i>regina</i> (<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> for <i>king</i> and <i>queen</i>, respectively). The present monarch's signature is "Elizabeth R". From 1877 until 1948 reigning monarchs added the letter I to their signatures, for <i>imperator</i> or <i>imperatrix</i> (<i>emperor</i> or <i>empress</i> in Latin), from their status as <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_India" title="Emperor of India">Emperor or Empress of India</a>. For example, Queen Victoria signed as "Victoria RI" from 1877.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Arms">Arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Royal_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom">Royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom">Royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom</a> are "Quarterly, I and IV Gules three lions passant guardant in pale Or [for England]; II Or a lion rampant within a double tressure flory-counter-flory Gules [for Scotland]; III Azure a harp Or stringed Argent [for Ireland]". The supporters are <a href="/wiki/The_Lion_and_the_Unicorn" title="The Lion and the Unicorn">the Lion and the Unicorn</a>; the motto is "<a href="/wiki/Dieu_et_mon_droit" title="Dieu et mon droit">Dieu et mon droit</a>" (French: "God and my Right"). Surrounding the shield is a representation of a <a href="/wiki/Garter_(stockings)" title="Garter (stockings)">Garter</a> bearing the motto of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chivalric_order" title="Chivalric order">Chivalric</a> <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Garter" title="Order of the Garter">order</a> of the same name; "<a href="/wiki/Honi_soit_qui_mal_y_pense" title="Honi soit qui mal y pense">Honi soit qui mal y pense</a>". (<a href="/wiki/Old_French" title="Old French">Old French</a>: "Shame be to him who thinks evil of it"). In Scotland, the monarch uses an alternative form of the arms in which quarters I and IV represent Scotland, II England, and III Ireland. The mottoes are "In Defens" (an abbreviated form of the <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a> "<a href="/wiki/In_My_Defens_God_Me_Defend" title="In My Defens God Me Defend">In My Defens God Me Defend</a>") and the motto of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Thistle" title="Order of the Thistle">Order of the Thistle</a>; "<a href="/wiki/Nemo_me_impune_lacessit" title="Nemo me impune lacessit">Nemo me impune lacessit</a>". (<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>: "No-one provokes me with impunity"); the supporters are the unicorn and lion, who support both the <a href="/wiki/Escutcheon_(heraldry)" title="Escutcheon (heraldry)">escutcheon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lance" title="Lance">lances</a>, from which fly the flags of <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Scotland" title="Flag of Scotland">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_England" title="Flag of England">England</a>.</p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:602px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_(Both_Realms).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1517" height="297" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%28Both_Realms%29.svg/600px-Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%28Both_Realms%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%28Both_Realms%29.svg/900px-Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%28Both_Realms%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%28Both_Realms%29.svg/1200px-Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%28Both_Realms%29.svg.png 2x" width="600"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_(Both_Realms).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Royal_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom">coat of arms</a> of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> in the United Kingdom. The design, in use since the accession of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> in 1837, features the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Arms_of_England" title="Royal Arms of England">arms of England</a> in the first and fourth quarters, <a href="/wiki/Royal_coat_of_arms_of_Scotland" title="Royal coat of arms of Scotland">Scotland</a> in the second, and <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Ireland" title="Coat of arms of Ireland">Ireland</a> in the third. In <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> a separate version is used (shown right) whereby the Arms of Scotland take precedence.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The monarch's official flag in the United Kingdom is the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Standard_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal Standard of the United Kingdom">Royal Standard</a>, which depicts the Royal Arms in <a href="/wiki/Banner_of_arms" title="Banner of arms">banner form</a>. It is flown only from buildings, vessels and vehicles in which the Sovereign is present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jack_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-jack-123">[123]</a></sup> The Royal Standard is never flown at half-mast because there is always a sovereign: when one dies, his or her successor becomes the sovereign instantly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<p>When the monarch is not in residence, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Flag" title="Union Flag">Union Flag</a> is flown at <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Castle" title="Windsor Castle">Windsor Castle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sandringham_House" title="Sandringham House">Sandringham House</a>, whereas in Scotland the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Standard_of_Scotland" title="Royal Standard of Scotland">Royal Standard of Scotland</a> is flown at <a href="/wiki/Holyrood_Palace" title="Holyrood Palace">Holyrood Palace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balmoral_Castle" title="Balmoral Castle">Balmoral Castle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jack_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-jack-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<center>
<table style="background:transparent;margin-top:0.5em">
<tr>
<td>
<table style="width:220px;float:left;border-collapse:collapse;margin:3px">
<tr>

<dd><sup>2</sup> <span class="wrap">Dominion, never ratified <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster 1931</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commission_of_Government" title="Commission of Government">London-based external government</a> 1934–1949, annexed by Canada in 1949</span></dd>
<dd><sup>3</sup> <span class="wrap"><a href="/wiki/Rhodesia%27s_Unilateral_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Rhodesia's Unilateral Declaration of Independence">Rhodesia unilaterally declared independence</a> as a realm in 1965, but this was not recognised internationally. Declared itself a republic in 1970.</span></dd>
